<li><i><b><a href="//en.wikinews.org/wiki/Apple_to_give_free_cases,_refunds_to_iPhone_4_owners" class="extiw" title="wikinews:Apple to give free cases, refunds to iPhone 4 owners">Apple to give free cases, refunds to iPhone 4 owners</a></b></i></li>
<li><i><b><a href="//en.wikinews.org/wiki/Apple_unveils_new_iPods,_Apple_TV;_updates_iOS,_iTunes" class="extiw" title="wikinews:Apple unveils new iPods, Apple TV; updates iOS, iTunes">Apple unveils new iPods, Apple TV; updates iOS, iTunes</a></b></i></li>
<li><i><b><a href="//en.wikinews.org/wiki/Apple_unveils_new_MacBook_Air_laptops,_iLife_%2711_software_suite" class="extiw" title="wikinews:Apple unveils new MacBook Air laptops, iLife '11 software suite">Apple unveils new MacBook Air laptops, iLife '11 software suite</a></b></i></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>After years of speculation and multiple rumored "leaks", Apple announced a large screen, tablet-like media device known as the iPad on January 27, 2010. The iPad ran the same touch-based operating system as the iPhone, and many iPhone apps were compatible with the iPad. This gave the iPad a large app catalog on launch, despite very little development time before the release. Later that year on April 3, 2010, the iPad was launched in the US. It sold more than 300,000 units on its first day, and 500,000 by the end of the first week.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> In May of the same year, Apple's <a href="/wiki/Market_cap" title="Market cap" class="mw-redirect">market cap</a> exceeded that of competitor <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> for the first time since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2010, Apple released the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4" title="IPhone 4">iPhone 4</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> which introduced <a href="/wiki/Video_calling" title="Video calling" class="mw-redirect">video calling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_multitasking" title="Computer multitasking">multitasking</a>, and a new <a href="/wiki/Electrical_insulation" title="Electrical insulation" class="mw-redirect">uninsulated</a> <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a> design that acted as the phone's antenna. Later that year, Apple again refreshed its iPod line of MP3 players by introducing a <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">multi-touch</a> <a href="/wiki/IPod_Nano" title="IPod Nano">iPod Nano</a>, an <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a> with <a href="/wiki/FaceTime" title="FaceTime">FaceTime</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/IPod_Shuffle" title="IPod Shuffle">iPod Shuffle</a> that brought back the buttons of earlier generations.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo1_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo1-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, on October 20, Apple updated the <a href="/wiki/MacBook_Air" title="MacBook Air">MacBook Air</a> laptop, <a href="/wiki/ILife" title="ILife">iLife</a> suite of applications, and unveiled <a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X_Lion" title="Mac OS X Lion">Mac OS X Lion</a>, the last version with the name <i><a href="/wiki/Mac_OS_X" title="Mac OS X" class="mw-redirect">Mac OS X</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-october20releasepcmag_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-october20releasepcmag-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2010, Apple shares hit an all-time high, eclipsing $300.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_Store_Yonkers,_NY_January_8,_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Apple_Store_Yonkers%2C_NY_January_8%2C_2013.jpg/220px-Apple_Store_Yonkers%2C_NY_January_8%2C_2013.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Apple_Store_Yonkers%2C_NY_January_8%2C_2013.jpg/330px-Apple_Store_Yonkers%2C_NY_January_8%2C_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Apple_Store_Yonkers%2C_NY_January_8%2C_2013.jpg/440px-Apple_Store_Yonkers%2C_NY_January_8%2C_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2281" data-file-height="1539" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_Store_Yonkers,_NY_January_8,_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Apple_Store" title="Apple Store">Apple Store</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yonkers" title="Yonkers" class="mw-redirect">Yonkers</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On January 6, 2011, the company opened its <a href="/wiki/Mac_App_Store" title="Mac App Store">Mac App Store</a>, a digital software distribution platform similar to the iOS App Store.<sup id="cite_ref-1-6-10-PCMAG-MACAPPSTORE_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1-6-10-PCMAG-MACAPPSTORE-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Alongside peer entities such as Atari and Cisco Systems, Apple was featured in the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Something_Ventured_(film)" title="Something Ventured (film)" class="mw-redirect">Something Ventured</a></i> which premiered in 2011 and explored the three-decade era that led to the establishment and dominance of Silicon Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On January 17, 2011, Jobs announced in an internal Apple memo that he would take another medical leave of absence, for an indefinite period, to allow him to focus on his health. Chief operating officer <a href="/wiki/Tim_Cook" title="Tim Cook">Tim Cook</a> assumed Jobs's day-to-day operations at Apple, although Jobs would still remain "involved in major strategic decisions".<sup id="cite_ref-JobsLeave2011_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JobsLeave2011-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple became the most valuable consumer-facing brand in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2011, Jobs surprisingly took the stage and unveiled <a href="/wiki/ICloud" title="ICloud">iCloud</a>, an online storage and syncing service for music, photos, files and software which replaced MobileMe, Apple's previous attempt at content syncing.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>This would be the last product launch Jobs would attend before his death. It has been argued that Apple has achieved such efficiency in its supply chain that the company operates as a <a href="/wiki/Monopsony" title="Monopsony">monopsony</a> (one buyer, many sellers) and can dictate terms to its suppliers.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-supply_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supply-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> In July 2011, due to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_debt-ceiling_crisis_of_2011" title="United States debt-ceiling crisis of 2011">American debt-ceiling crisis</a>, Apple's financial reserves were briefly larger than those of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">U.S. Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On August 24, 2011, Jobs resigned his position as CEO of Apple.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> He was replaced by Cook and Jobs became Apple's chairman. Prior to this, Apple did not have a chairman and instead had two co-lead directors, <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Jung" title="Andrea Jung">Andrea Jung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_D._Levinson" title="Arthur D. Levinson">Arthur D. Levinson</a>, who continued with those titles until Levinson became Chairman of the Board in November.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.93present:_Post-Jobs_era">2011–present: Post-Jobs era</span></h3>
<p>On October 5, 2011, Apple announced that Jobs had died, marking the end of an era for Apple.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-press_release_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press_release-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> The first major product announcement by Apple following Jobs's passing occurred on January 19, 2012, when Apple's <a href="/wiki/Phil_Schiller" title="Phil Schiller">Phil Schiller</a> introduced iBooks Textbooks for iOS and iBook Author for Mac OS X in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Jobs had stated in his biography that he wanted to reinvent the textbook industry and education.</p>
<p>From 2011 to 2012, Apple released the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4S" title="IPhone 4S">iPhone 4S</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5" title="IPhone 5">iPhone 5</a>, which featured improved cameras, an "<a href="/wiki/Intelligent_personal_assistant" title="Intelligent personal assistant">intelligent software assistant</a>" named <a href="/wiki/Siri" title="Siri">Siri</a>, and cloud-sourced data with iCloud;<sup id="cite_ref-iP4S_US_unlocked_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iP4S_US_unlocked-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dan_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dan-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/IPad_(third_generation)" title="IPad (third generation)" class="mw-redirect">third</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPad_(fourth_generation)" title="IPad (fourth generation)" class="mw-redirect">fourth</a> generation iPads, which featured <a href="/wiki/Retina_Display" title="Retina Display">Retina displays</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/IPad_Mini" title="IPad Mini">iPad Mini</a>, which featured a 7.9-inch screen in contrast to the iPad's 9.7-inch screen.<sup id="cite_ref-mini_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mini-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> These launches were successful, with the iPhone 5 (released September 21, 2012) becoming Apple's biggest iPhone launch with over 2 million pre-orders<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> and sales of 3 million iPads in three days following the launch of the iPad Mini and fourth generation iPad (released November 3, 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple also released a third-generation 13-inch <a href="/wiki/MacBook_Pro" title="MacBook Pro">MacBook Pro</a> with a Retina display and new <a href="/wiki/IMac" title="IMac">iMac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mac_Mini" title="Mac Mini">Mac Mini</a> computers.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mini_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mini-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On October 29, 2011, Apple purchased C3 Technologies, a mapping company, for $240 million, becoming the third mapping company Apple has purchased.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> On January 10, 2012, Apple paid $500 million to acquire <a href="/wiki/Anobit" title="Anobit">Anobit</a>, an Israeli hardware company that developed and supplied a proprietary memory signal processing technology that improved the performance of the flash-memory used in iPhones and iPads.<sup id="cite_ref-Apple_buys_Israeli_technology_firm_Anobit_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apple_buys_Israeli_technology_firm_Anobit-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 24, 2012, during a conference call with investors, Tim Cook said that he loved <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, but that Apple was going to expect larger opportunities outside of India. Cook cited the reason as the 30% sourcing requirement from India.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On August 20, 2012, Apple's rising stock rose the company's value to a world-record $624 billion. This beat the non-inflation-adjusted record for market capitalization set by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> On August 24, 2012, a US jury ruled that Samsung should pay Apple $1.05 billion (£665m) in damages in an <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property" title="Intellectual property">intellectual property</a> lawsuit.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Samsung appealed the damages award, which the Court reduced by $450 million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOSS_Patents_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOSS_Patents-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> The Court further granted Samsung's request for a new trial.<sup id="cite_ref-FOSS_Patents_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOSS_Patents-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> On November 10, 2012, Apple confirmed a global settlement that would dismiss all lawsuits between Apple and HTC up to that date, in favor of a ten-year license agreement for current and future patents between the two companies.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> It is predicted that Apple will make $280 million a year from this deal with HTC.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mergers_and_acquisitions_by_Apple" title="List of mergers and acquisitions by Apple">List of mergers and acquisitions by Apple</a></div>
<p>A previously confidential email written by Jobs a year before his death, was presented during the proceedings of the <i><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc._v._Samsung_Electronics_Co." title="Apple Inc. v. Samsung Electronics Co.">Apple Inc. v. Samsung Electronics Co.</a></i> lawsuits and became publicly available in early April 2014. With a subject line that reads "Top 100&#160;– A," the email was sent only to the company's 100 most senior employees and outlines Jobs's vision of Apple Inc.'s future under 10 subheadings. Notably, Jobs declares a "Holy War with Google" for 2011 and schedules a "new campus" for 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2013, Apple filed a patent for an augmented reality (AR) system that can identify objects in a live video stream and present information corresponding to these objects through a computer-generated information layer overlaid on top of the real-world image.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> Later in 2013, Apple acquired Embark Inc., a small Silicon Valley-based mapping company that builds free transit apps to help smartphone users navigate public transportation in U.S. cities,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/PrimeSense" title="PrimeSense">PrimeSense</a>, an Israeli 3D sensing company based in Tel Aviv.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2013, Apple Inc. purchased social analytics firm Topsy. Topsy is one of a small number of firms with real-time access to the messages that appear on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> and can "do real-time analysis of the trends and discussions happening on Twitter".<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> The company also made several high profile hiring decisions in 2013. On July 2, 2013, Apple recruited <a href="/wiki/Paul_Deneve" title="Paul Deneve">Paul Deneve</a>, Belgian President and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Yves_Saint_Laurent_(brand)" title="Yves Saint Laurent (brand)">Yves Saint Laurent</a> as a vice president reporting directly to Tim Cook.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> A mid-October 2013 announcement revealed that <a href="/wiki/Burberry" title="Burberry">Burberry</a> executive <a href="/wiki/Angela_Ahrendts" title="Angela Ahrendts">Angela Ahrendts</a> will commence as a senior vice president at Apple in mid-2014. Ahrendts oversaw Burberry's digital strategy for almost eight years and, during her tenure, sales increased to about US$3.2 billion and shares gained more than threefold.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the Worldwide Developer's Conference on June 10, 2013, Apple announced the <a href="/wiki/IOS_7" title="IOS 7">seventh iOS</a> operating system alongside <a href="/wiki/OS_X_Mavericks" title="OS X Mavericks">OS X Mavericks</a>, the tenth version of Mac OS X, and a new <a href="/wiki/Internet_radio" title="Internet radio">Internet radio</a> service called <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Radio" title="ITunes Radio">iTunes Radio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-theverge_mavericks_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theverge_mavericks-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theverge_ios7_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theverge_ios7-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theverge_iradio_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theverge_iradio-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> iTunes Radio, iOS 7 and OS X Mavericks were released fall 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-theverge_mavericks_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theverge_mavericks-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theverge_ios7_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theverge_ios7-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> On December 6, 2013, Apple Inc. launched <a href="/wiki/IBeacon" title="IBeacon">iBeacon</a> across its 254 U.S. retail stores. Using Bluetooth wireless technology, iBeacon senses the user's exact location within the <a href="/wiki/Apple_store" title="Apple store" class="mw-redirect">Apple store</a> and sends the user messages about products, events and other information, tailored to the user's location.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Alongside Google vice-president Vint Cerf and AT&amp;T CEO Randall Stephenson, Cook attended a closed-door summit held by President Obama on August 8, 2013, in regard to government surveillance and the Internet in the wake of the Edward Snowden <a href="/wiki/Global_surveillance_disclosures_(2013%E2%80%93present)" title="Global surveillance disclosures (2013–present)">NSA incident</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 4, 2014, Cook met with <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_G%C3%BCl" title="Abdullah Gül">Abdullah Gül</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Turkey" title="President of Turkey">President of Turkey</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a> to discuss the company's involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Fatih_project" title="Fatih project">Fatih project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> Cook also confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>'s first Apple Retail Store would be opened in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> in April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>An anonymous Apple employee revealed to the <i>Bloomberg</i> media publication that the opening of a <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, Japan, store was planned for 2014. A Japanese analyst has stated, "For Apple, the Japanese market is appealing in terms of quantity and price. There is room to expand tablet sales and a possibility the Japanese market expands if Apple’s mobile carrier partners increase."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 13, 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Apple operated three stores in Tokyo.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 1, 2013, Apple India executives unveiled a plan to expand further into the Indian market, following Cook's acknowledgment of the country in July 2013 when sales results showed that iPhone sales in India grew 400% during the second quarter of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Apple Inc. reported that the company sold 51 million iPhones in the Q1 of 2014 (an all-time quarterly record), compared to 47.8 million in the year-ago quarter. Apple also sold 26 million iPads during the quarter, also an all-time quarterly record, compared to 22.9 million in the year-ago quarter. The Company sold 4.8 million Macs, compared to 4.1 million in the year-ago quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 28, 2014, Apple confirmed its intent to acquire <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a>'s audio company <a href="/wiki/Beats_Electronics" title="Beats Electronics">Beats Electronics</a>—producer of the <i>Beats by Dr. Dre</i> line of headphones and speaker products, and operator of the music streaming service <a href="/wiki/Beats_Music" title="Beats Music">Beats Music</a>—for $3 billion, and to sell their products through Apple's retail outlets and resellers. Iovine felt that Beats had always "belonged" with Apple, as the company modeled itself after Apple's "unmatched ability to marry culture and technology."<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-verge-beatsappleconfirmed_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-beatsappleconfirmed-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-apple-pr_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apple-pr-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2014, an Apple representative confirmed to the media that <a href="/wiki/Anand_Lal_Shimpi" title="Anand Lal Shimpi">Anand Lal Shimpi</a>, editor and publisher of the <i>AnandTech</i> website, had been recruited by Apple without elaborating on Lal Shimpi's role.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Apple_products" title="Timeline of Apple products" class="mw-redirect">Timeline of Apple products</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_products_discontinued_by_Apple_Inc." title="List of products discontinued by Apple Inc.">List of products discontinued by Apple Inc.</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mac">Mac</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Macintosh" title="Macintosh">Macintosh</a></div>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Macintosh_models" title="Timeline of Macintosh models">Timeline of Macintosh models</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Macintosh_models_grouped_by_CPU_type" title="List of Macintosh models grouped by CPU type">List of Macintosh models grouped by CPU type</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Macintosh_models_by_case_type" title="List of Macintosh models by case type">List of Macintosh models by case type</a></div>
<p>Macs that are currently being sold are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/MacBook_(2015_version)" title="MacBook (2015 version)" class="mw-redirect">MacBook</a>: Consumer ultra-thin, ultra-portable notebook, introduced in 2006 and relaunched in 2015.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MacBook_Air" title="MacBook Air">MacBook Air</a>: Consumer ultra-thin, ultra-portable notebook, introduced in 2008.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MacBook_Pro" title="MacBook Pro">MacBook Pro</a>: Professional notebook, introduced in 2006.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mac_Mini" title="Mac Mini">Mac Mini</a>: Consumer sub-desktop computer, introduced in 2005.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IMac" title="IMac">iMac</a>: Consumer all-in one desktop computer, introduced in 1998.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mac_Pro" title="Mac Pro">Mac Pro</a>: Workstation desktop computer, introduced in 2006.</li>
</ul>
<p>Apple sells a variety of computer accessories for Macs, including <a href="/wiki/Apple_Thunderbolt_Display" title="Apple Thunderbolt Display">Thunderbolt Display</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magic_Mouse" title="Magic Mouse">Magic Mouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magic_Trackpad" title="Magic Trackpad">Magic Trackpad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Wireless_Keyboard" title="Apple Wireless Keyboard">Wireless Keyboard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Battery_Charger" title="Apple Battery Charger">Battery Charger</a>, the AirPort wireless networking products, and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Time_Capsule" title="Apple Time Capsule" class="mw-redirect">Time Capsule</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="iPod">iPod</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPod</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IPod_line_as_of_2014.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/IPod_line_as_of_2014.png/220px-IPod_line_as_of_2014.png" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/IPod_line_as_of_2014.png/330px-IPod_line_as_of_2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/IPod_line_as_of_2014.png/440px-IPod_line_as_of_2014.png 2x" data-file-width="703" data-file-height="604" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IPod_line_as_of_2014.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
iPod line as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. From left to right: <a href="/wiki/IPod_Shuffle" title="IPod Shuffle">iPod Shuffle</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPod_Nano" title="IPod Nano">iPod Nano</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On October 23, 2001, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPod</a> digital music player. Several updated models have since been introduced, and the iPod brand is now the market leader in portable music players by a significant margin. More than 350 million units have shipped as of September 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple has partnered with <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> to offer the <a href="/wiki/Nike%2BiPod" title="Nike+iPod" class="mw-redirect">Nike+iPod</a> Sports Kit, enabling runners to synchronize and monitor their runs with iTunes and the Nike+ website.</p>
<p>Apple currently sells three variants of the iPod:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/IPod_Shuffle" title="IPod Shuffle">iPod Shuffle</a>: Ultra-portable digital audio player, currently available in a 2&#160;GB model, introduced in 2005.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IPod_Nano" title="IPod Nano">iPod Nano</a>: <a href="/wiki/Portable_media_player" title="Portable media player">Portable media player</a>, currently available in a 16&#160;GB model, introduced in 2005. Earlier models featured the traditional <a href="/wiki/IPod_click_wheel" title="IPod click wheel">iPod click wheel</a>, but the current generation features a <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">multi-touch</a> interface and includes an <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" title="FM radio" class="mw-redirect">FM radio</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Pedometer" title="Pedometer">pedometer</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a>: Portable media player that runs <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and is currently available in 16, 32, 64, and 128&#160;GB models, introduced in 2007. The <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch_(6th_generation)" title="IPod Touch (6th generation)">current generation</a> features the <a href="/wiki/Apple_A8" title="Apple A8">Apple A8</a> processor, a <a href="/wiki/Retina_display" title="Retina display" class="mw-redirect">Retina display</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siri" title="Siri">Siri</a> and dual cameras on the front (1.2 megapixel sensor) and back (8 megapixel <a href="/wiki/ISight" title="ISight">iSight</a>). The latter camera supports HD <a href="/wiki/Video_recording" title="Video recording" class="mw-redirect">video recording</a> at <a href="/wiki/1080p" title="1080p">1080p</a> and slow motion video at 120fps in 720p.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="iPhone">iPhone</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IPhone_montage.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/IPhone_montage.png/150px-IPhone_montage.png" width="150" height="409" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/IPhone_montage.png/225px-IPhone_montage.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/IPhone_montage.png/300px-IPhone_montage.png 2x" data-file-width="828" data-file-height="2256" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IPhone_montage.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/IPhone_(first_generation)" title="IPhone (first generation)" class="mw-redirect">first-generation iPhone</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPhone_3G" title="IPhone 3G">3G</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4" title="IPhone 4">4</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5" title="IPhone 5">5</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5C" title="IPhone 5C">5C</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5S" title="IPhone 5S">5S</a> to scale.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Macworld_Conference_%26_Expo" title="Macworld Conference &amp; Expo" class="mw-redirect">Macworld Conference &amp; Expo</a> in January 2007, Steve Jobs introduced the long-anticipated<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>, a convergence of an Internet-enabled <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> and iPod.<sup id="cite_ref-apple.com_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apple.com-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IPhone_(first_generation)" title="IPhone (first generation)" class="mw-redirect">first-generation iPhone</a> was released on June 29, 2007 for $499 (4&#160;GB) and $599 (8&#160;GB) with an <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Inc." title="AT&amp;T Inc." class="mw-redirect">AT&amp;T</a> contract.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 5, 2008, it was updated to have 16&#160;GB of memory, in addition to the 8&#160;GB and 4&#160;GB models.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> It combined a <a href="/wiki/2.5G" title="2.5G" class="mw-redirect">2.5G</a> <a href="/wiki/Quad_band" title="Quad band" class="mw-redirect">quad band</a> <a href="/wiki/Global_System_for_Mobile_Communications" title="Global System for Mobile Communications" class="mw-redirect">GSM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Data_Rates_for_GSM_Evolution" title="Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution">EDGE</a> cellular phone with features found in handheld devices, running scaled-down versions of Apple's Mac OS X (dubbed iPhone OS, later renamed <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>), with various Mac OS X applications such as <a href="/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)" title="Safari (web browser)">Safari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mail_(OS_X)" title="Mail (OS X)" class="mw-redirect">Mail</a>. It also includes web-based and <a href="/wiki/Dashboard_(Mac_OS)" title="Dashboard (Mac OS)">Dashboard</a> apps such as <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dashboard_(Mac_OS)" title="Dashboard (Mac OS)">Weather</a>. The iPhone features a 3.5-inch (89&#160;mm) touchscreen display, <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth" title="Bluetooth">Bluetooth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> (both "b" and "g").<sup id="cite_ref-apple.com_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apple.com-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A second version, the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_3G" title="IPhone 3G">iPhone 3G</a>, was released on July 11, 2008 with a reduced price of $199 for the 8&#160;GB version and $299 for the 16&#160;GB version.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> This version added support for <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> networking and <a href="/wiki/Assisted-GPS" title="Assisted-GPS" class="mw-redirect">assisted-GPS</a> navigation. The flat silver back and large antenna square of the original model were eliminated in favor of a glossy, curved black or white back. Software capabilities were improved with the release of the <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a>, which provided iPhone-compatible applications to download. On April 24, 2009, the App Store <sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> surpassed one billion downloads.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> On June 8, 2009, Apple announced the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_3GS" title="IPhone 3GS">iPhone 3GS</a>. It provided an incremental update to the device, including faster internal components, support for faster 3G speeds, video recording capability, and voice control.</p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Worldwide_Developers_Conference" title="Apple Worldwide Developers Conference">Worldwide Developers Conference</a> (WWDC) on June 7, 2010, Apple announced the redesigned <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4" title="IPhone 4">iPhone 4</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> It featured a 960x640 display, the <a href="/wiki/Apple_A4" title="Apple A4">Apple A4</a> processor, a <a href="/wiki/Gyroscope" title="Gyroscope">gyroscope</a> for enhanced gaming, a 5MP camera with LED flash, front-facing <a href="/wiki/VGA" title="VGA" class="mw-redirect">VGA</a> camera and <a href="/wiki/FaceTime" title="FaceTime">FaceTime</a> video calling. Shortly after its release, reception issues were discovered by consumers, due to the stainless steel band around the edge of the device, which also serves as the phone's cellular signal and Wi-Fi antenna. The issue was corrected by a "Bumper Case" distributed by Apple for free to all owners for a few months. In June 2011, Apple overtook <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> to become the world's biggest smartphone maker by volume.<sup id="cite_ref-ftover_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ftover-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 4, 2011, Apple unveiled the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4S" title="IPhone 4S">iPhone 4S</a>, which was first released on October 14, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> It features the <a href="/wiki/Apple_A5" title="Apple A5">Apple A5</a> processor and <a href="/wiki/Siri" title="Siri">Siri</a> voice assistant technology, the latter of which Apple had acquired in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> It also features an updated 8MP camera with new optics. Apple sold 4 million iPhone 4S phones in the first three days of availability.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On September 12, 2012, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5" title="IPhone 5">iPhone 5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> It added a 4-inch display, 4G LTE connectivity, and the upgraded <a href="/wiki/Apple_A6" title="Apple A6">Apple A6</a> chip, among several other improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Two million iPhones were sold in the first twenty-four hours of pre-ordering<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> and over five million handsets were sold in the first three days of its launch.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon the launch of the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5S" title="IPhone 5S">iPhone 5S</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5C" title="IPhone 5C">iPhone 5C</a>, Apple set a new record for first-weekend smartphone sales by selling over nine million devices in the first three days of its launch.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> The release of the iPhone 5S and 5C was the first time that Apple simultaneously launched two models.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A patent filed in July 2013 revealed the development of a new iPhone battery system that uses location data in combination with data on the user's habits to moderate the handsets power settings accordingly. Apple is working towards a power management system that will provide features such as the ability of the iPhone to estimate the length of time a user will be away from a power source to modify energy usage and a detection function that adjusts the charging rate to best suit the type of power source that is being used.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a March 2014 interview, Apple designer <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Ive" title="Jonathan Ive">Jonathan Ive</a> used the iPhone as an example of Apple's ethos of creating high-quality, life-changing products. He explained that the phones are comparatively expensive due to the intensive effort that is used to make them:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>We don’t take so long and make the way we make for fiscal reasons ... Quite the reverse. The body is made from a single piece of machined aluminium ... The whole thing is polished first to a mirror finish and then is very finely textured, except for the Apple logo. The chamfers [smoothed-off edges] are cut with diamond-tipped cutters. The cutters don’t usually last very long, so we had to figure out a way of mass-manufacturing long-lasting ones. The camera cover is sapphire crystal. Look at the details around the sim-card slot. It’s extraordinary!<sup id="cite_ref-Time_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>On September 9, 2014, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_6" title="IPhone 6">iPhone 6</a>, alongside the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_6_Plus" title="IPhone 6 Plus" class="mw-redirect">iPhone 6 Plus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> One year later, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_6s" title="IPhone 6s" class="mw-redirect">iPhone 6s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IPhone_6s_Plus" title="IPhone 6s Plus" class="mw-redirect">iPhone 6s Plus</a>, which introduced a new technology called 3DTouch, including an increase of the rear camera to 12 MP, and the FaceTime camera to 5 MP.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="iPad">iPad</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a></div>
<p>On January 27, 2010, Apple introduced their much-anticipated media <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet</a>, the <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a>, which runs a modified version of iOS. It offers multi-touch interaction with multimedia formats including newspapers, ebooks, photos, videos, music, word processing documents, video games, and most existing iPhone apps.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> It also includes a mobile version of <a href="/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)" title="Safari (web browser)">Safari</a> for web browsing, as well as access to the App Store, <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> Library, <a href="/wiki/IBooks" title="IBooks">iBookstore</a>, Contacts, and Notes. Content is downloadable via <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> and optional <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> service or synced through the user's computer.<sup id="cite_ref-MacRumors-iPad-event_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacRumors-iPad-event-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Inc." title="AT&amp;T Inc." class="mw-redirect">AT&amp;T</a> was initially the sole U.S. provider of 3G wireless access for the iPad.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On March 2, 2011, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPad_2" title="IPad 2" class="mw-redirect">iPad 2</a>, which had a faster processor and a camera on the front and back. It also added support for optional 3G service provided by <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon</a> in addition to <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Inc." title="AT&amp;T Inc." class="mw-redirect">AT&amp;T</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes-ipad2_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-ipad2-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> The availability of the iPad 2 was initially limited as a result of a devastating <a href="/wiki/2011_T%C5%8Dhoku_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2011 Tōhoku earthquake and tsunami">earthquake and tsunami</a> in Japan in March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> The third-generation iPad was released on March 7, 2012 and marketed as "<a href="/wiki/IPad_(third_generation)" title="IPad (third generation)" class="mw-redirect">the new iPad</a>". It added <a href="/wiki/3GPP_Long_Term_Evolution" title="3GPP Long Term Evolution" class="mw-redirect">LTE</a> service from AT&amp;T or Verizon, an upgraded <a href="/wiki/A5X" title="A5X" class="mw-redirect">A5X</a> processor, and Retina display. The dimensions and form factor remained relatively unchanged, with the new iPad being a fraction thicker and heavier than the previous version and featuring minor positioning changes.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On October 23, 2012, Apple's fourth-generation iPad came out, marketed as the "<a href="/wiki/IPad_(fourth_generation)" title="IPad (fourth generation)" class="mw-redirect">iPad with Retina display</a>". It added the upgraded <a href="/wiki/A6X" title="A6X" class="mw-redirect">A6X</a> processor and replaced the traditional 30-pin dock connector with the all-digital <a href="/wiki/Lightning_(connector)" title="Lightning (connector)">Lightning connector</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IPad_Mini" title="IPad Mini">iPad Mini</a> was also introduced. It featured a reduced 7.9-inch display and much of the same internal specifications as the iPad 2.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 22, 2013, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPad_Air" title="IPad Air">iPad Air</a> and the iPad mini with Retina Display, both featuring a new 64 bit Apple-A7 processor.<sup id="cite_ref-iPad_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iPad-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IPad_Air_2" title="IPad Air 2">iPad Air 2</a> was unveiled on October 16, 2014. It added better graphics and central processing and a camera burst mode as well as minor updates. The <a href="/wiki/IPad_Mini_3" title="IPad Mini 3">iPad Mini 3</a> was unveiled at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-iPad_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iPad-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Since its launch, iPad users have downloaded three billion apps. The total number of App Store downloads is over 75 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75bill_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75bill-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Apple_Watch">Apple Watch</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apple_Watch" title="Apple Watch">Apple Watch</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_Watch-.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Apple_Watch-.jpg/220px-Apple_Watch-.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Apple_Watch-.jpg/330px-Apple_Watch-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Apple_Watch-.jpg/440px-Apple_Watch-.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4700" data-file-height="3133" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_Watch-.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Apple Watch quickly became the best-selling wearable device, with the shipment of 11.4 million smart watches in the first half of 2015, according to analyst firm Canalys.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Apple Watch <a href="/wiki/Smartwatch" title="Smartwatch">smartwatch</a> was launched by Cook on September 9, 2014, and released on April 24, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> The wearable device consists of fitness-tracking capabilities that are similar to <a href="/wiki/Fitbit" title="Fitbit">Fitbit</a>, and must be used in combination with an iPhone to work (only the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5" title="IPhone 5">iPhone 5</a>, or later models, are compatible with the Apple Watch).<sup id="cite_ref-pressrelease_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pressrelease-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-applewatchtech_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-applewatchtech-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theverge_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theverge-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Apple_TV">Apple TV</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a></div>
<p>At the 2007 Macworld conference, Jobs demonstrated the <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a> (previously known as the iTV),<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> a set-top video device intended to bridge the sale of content from iTunes with high-definition televisions. The device links up to a user's TV and syncs, either via Wi-Fi or a wired network, with one computer's iTunes library and streams content from an additional four. The Apple TV originally incorporated a 40&#160;GB hard drive for storage, included outputs for <a href="/wiki/HDMI" title="HDMI">HDMI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Component_video" title="Component video">component video</a>, and played video at a maximum resolution of <a href="/wiki/720p" title="720p">720p</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 31, 2007, a 160 GB drive was released alongside the existing 40&#160;GB model.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> A software update released on January 15, 2008 allowed media to be purchased directly from the Apple TV.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2009, Apple discontinued the original 40 GB Apple TV and now continues to produce and sell the 160 GB Apple TV. On September 1, 2010, Apple released a completely redesigned Apple TV. The new device is 1/4 the size, runs quieter, and replaces the need for a hard drive with media streaming from any iTunes library on the network along with 8 GB of <a href="/wiki/Flash_memory" title="Flash memory">flash memory</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cache_(computing)" title="Cache (computing)">cache</a> media downloaded. Like the iPad and the iPhone, Apple TV runs on an A4 processor. The memory included in the device is half of that in the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4" title="IPhone 4">iPhone 4</a> at 256 MB; the same as the iPad, iPhone 3GS, third and fourth-generation <a href="/wiki/IPod_Touch" title="IPod Touch">iPod Touch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>It has HDMI out as the only video out source. Features include access to the iTunes Store to rent movies and TV shows (purchasing has been discontinued), streaming from internet video sources, including YouTube and Netflix, and media streaming from an iTunes library. Apple also reduced the price of the device to $99. A third generation of the device was introduced at an Apple event on March 7, 2012, with new features such as higher resolution (1080p) and a new user interface.</p>
<p>At the September 9, 2015 event, Apple unveiled an overhauled Apple TV, introducing the App Store and a new "<a href="/wiki/Siri" title="Siri">Siri</a> Remote" with a touchpad.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software">Software</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Macintosh_software" title="List of Macintosh software">List of Macintosh software</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg/220px-WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg/330px-WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg/440px-WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2575" data-file-height="1717" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WWDC_2011_Moscone_West_Exterior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Apple_Worldwide_Developers_Conference" title="Apple Worldwide Developers Conference">Apple Worldwide Developers Conference</a> is held annually by Apple to showcase its new software and technologies for software developers.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Apple develops its own <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> to run on Macs, <a href="/wiki/OS_X" title="OS X">OS X</a>, the latest version being <a href="/wiki/OS_X_El_Capitan" title="OS X El Capitan">OS X El Capitan</a> (version 10.11). Apple also independently develops computer software titles for its OS X operating system. Much of the software Apple develops is bundled with its computers. An example of this is the consumer-oriented iLife software package that bundles <a href="/wiki/IMovie" title="IMovie">iMovie</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPhoto" title="IPhoto">iPhoto</a> and <a href="/wiki/GarageBand" title="GarageBand">GarageBand</a>. For presentation, page layout and word processing, <a href="/wiki/IWork" title="IWork">iWork</a> is available, which includes <a href="/wiki/Keynote_(presentation_software)" title="Keynote (presentation software)">Keynote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pages_(iWork)" title="Pages (iWork)" class="mw-redirect">Pages</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Numbers_(software)" title="Numbers (software)" class="mw-redirect">Numbers</a>. iTunes, <a href="/wiki/QuickTime" title="QuickTime">QuickTime</a> media player, and <a href="/wiki/Software_Update" title="Software Update" class="mw-redirect">Software Update</a> are available as free downloads for both OS X and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a>.</p>
<p>Apple also offers a range of professional software titles. Their range of server software includes the operating system <a href="/wiki/OS_X_Server" title="OS X Server">OS X Server</a>; <a href="/wiki/Apple_Remote_Desktop" title="Apple Remote Desktop">Apple Remote Desktop</a>, a remote systems management application; and <a href="/wiki/Xsan" title="Xsan">Xsan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Storage_Area_Network" title="Storage Area Network" class="mw-redirect">Storage Area Network</a> file system. For the professional creative market, there is <a href="/wiki/Aperture_(software)" title="Aperture (software)">Aperture</a> for professional <a href="/wiki/Raw_image_format" title="Raw image format">RAW</a>-format <a href="/wiki/Photo" title="Photo" class="mw-redirect">photo</a> processing; <a href="/wiki/Final_Cut_Pro" title="Final Cut Pro">Final Cut Pro</a>, a video production suite; <a href="/wiki/Logic_Pro" title="Logic Pro">Logic Pro</a>, a comprehensive music toolkit; and <a href="/wiki/Motion_(software)" title="Motion (software)">Motion</a>, an advanced effects composition program.</p>
<p>Apple also offers online services with <a href="/wiki/ICloud" title="ICloud">iCloud</a>, which provides cloud storage and syncing for a wide range of data, including email, contacts, calendars, photos and documents. It also offers iOS device backup, and is able to integrate directly with third-party apps for even greater functionality. iCloud is the fourth generation of online services provided by Apple, and was preceded by <a href="/wiki/MobileMe" title="MobileMe">MobileMe</a>, .Mac and iTools, all which met varying degrees of success.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Apple_SIM">Apple SIM</span></h3>
<p>Apple launched a <a href="/wiki/Subscriber_identity_module" title="Subscriber identity module">SIM</a> card service that can be used by iPad owners in 90 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_vehicles">Electric vehicles</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apple_electric_car_project" title="Apple electric car project">Apple electric car project</a></div>
<p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Sydney_Morning_Herald" title="Sydney Morning Herald" class="mw-redirect">Sydney Morning Herald</a>,</i> Apple wants to start producing an <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric car</a> with <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_driving" title="Autonomous driving" class="mw-redirect">autonomous driving</a> as soon as 2020. Apple has made efforts to recruit battery experts and other electric automobile workers from <a href="/wiki/A123_Systems" title="A123 Systems">A123 Systems</a>, LG Chem, <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung Electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Controls" title="Johnson Controls">Johnson Controls</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_identity">Corporate identity</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Typography_of_Apple_Inc." title="Typography of Apple Inc.">Typography of Apple Inc.</a></div>
