</div>
</div>
<p>According to Steve Jobs, the company's name was inspired by his visit to an apple farm while on a <a href="/wiki/Fruitarian" title="Fruitarian" class="mw-redirect">fruitarian</a> diet. Jobs thought the name "Apple" was "fun, spirited and not intimidating".<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Apple's first logo, designed by Ron Wayne, depicts <a href="/wiki/Sir_Isaac_Newton" title="Sir Isaac Newton" class="mw-redirect">Sir Isaac Newton</a> sitting under an apple tree. It was almost immediately replaced by <a href="/wiki/Rob_Janoff" title="Rob Janoff">Rob Janoff</a>'s "rainbow Apple", the now-familiar rainbow-colored silhouette of an apple with a bite taken out of it. Janoff presented Jobs with several different monochromatic themes for the "bitten" logo, and Jobs immediately took a liking to it. However, Jobs insisted that the logo be colorized to humanize the company.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> The logo was designed with a bite so that it would not be confused with a cherry.<sup id="cite_ref-creativebits_interview_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-creativebits_interview-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> The colored stripes were conceived to make the logo more accessible, and to represent the fact the Apple II could generate graphics in color.<sup id="cite_ref-creativebits_interview_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-creativebits_interview-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> This logo is often erroneously referred to as a tribute to <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a>, with the bite mark a reference to <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing#Death" title="Alan Turing">his method of suicide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> Both Janoff and Apple deny any homage to Turing in the design of the logo.<sup id="cite_ref-creativebits_interview_225-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-creativebits_interview-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On August 27, 1999<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_221-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> (the year following the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/IMac_G3" title="IMac G3">iMac G3</a>), Apple officially dropped the rainbow scheme and began to use monochromatic logos nearly identical in shape to the previous rainbow incarnation. An <a href="/wiki/Aqua_(user_interface)" title="Aqua (user interface)">Aqua</a>-themed version of the monochrome logo was used from 1999 to 2003, and a glass-themed version was used from 2007 to 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Steve Jobs and Steve Wozniak were <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a> fans,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> but Apple Inc. had name and logo trademark issues with <a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps" title="Apple Corps">Apple Corps Ltd.</a>, a multimedia company started by the Beatles in 1967. This resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps_v_Apple_Computer" title="Apple Corps v Apple Computer">series of lawsuits</a> and tension between the two companies. These issues ended with settling of their most recent lawsuit in 2007.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising">Advertising</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc._advertising" title="Apple Inc. advertising">Apple Inc. advertising</a></div>
<p>Apple's first slogan, "<a href="/wiki/Byte" title="Byte">Byte</a> into an Apple", was coined in the late 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1997 to 2002, the slogan "<a href="/wiki/Think_Different" title="Think Different" class="mw-redirect">Think Different</a>" was used in advertising campaigns, and is still closely associated with Apple.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple also has slogans for specific product lines&#160;— for example, "iThink, therefore iMac" was used in 1998 to promote the iMac,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> and "Say hello to iPhone" has been used in iPhone advertisements.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> "Hello" was also used to introduce the original Macintosh, <a href="/wiki/Newton_(platform)" title="Newton (platform)" class="mw-redirect">Newton</a>, iMac ("hello (again)"), and iPod.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From the introduction of the Macintosh in 1984 with the <a href="/wiki/1984_(television_commercial)" title="1984 (television commercial)" class="mw-redirect">1984 Super Bowl commercial</a> to the more modern '<a href="/wiki/Get_a_Mac" title="Get a Mac">Get a Mac</a>' adverts, Apple has been recognized in for its efforts towards effective advertising and marketing for its products. However, claims made by later campaigns <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc._advertising#Criticism" title="Apple Inc. advertising">were criticized</a>, particularly the 2005 Power Mac ads.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple's product commercials gained a lot of attention as a result of their eye-popping graphics and catchy tunes.<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_News_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_News-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> Musicians who benefited from an improved profile as a result of their songs being included on Apple commercials include Canadian singer <a href="/wiki/Feist_(singer)" title="Feist (singer)">Feist</a> with the song "<a href="/wiki/1234_(song)" title="1234 (song)" class="mw-redirect">1234</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Yael_Naim" title="Yael Naim">Yael Naïm</a> with the song "<a href="/wiki/New_Soul" title="New Soul">New Soul</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_News_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_News-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_loyalty">Brand loyalty</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg/220px-Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg/330px-Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg/440px-Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="576" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ifc_shanghai_Apple_Store.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Apple aficionados wait in line around the Apple Store in anticipation of a new product.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"The scenes I witnessed at the opening of the new Apple store in London's <a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden" title="Covent Garden">Covent Garden</a> were more like an evangelical prayer meeting than a chance to buy a phone or a laptop."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>—<a href="/wiki/Alex_Riley_(comedian)" title="Alex Riley (comedian)">Alex Riley</a>, writing for the BBC<sup id="cite_ref-riley1_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riley1-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>Apple's high level of <a href="/wiki/Brand_loyalty" title="Brand loyalty">brand loyalty</a> is considered unusual for any product. <a href="/wiki/Apple_evangelist" title="Apple evangelist" class="mw-redirect">Apple evangelists</a> were actively engaged by the company at one time, but this was after the phenomenon had already been firmly established. Apple <a href="/wiki/Evangelism_marketing" title="Evangelism marketing">evangelist</a> <a href="/wiki/Guy_Kawasaki" title="Guy Kawasaki">Guy Kawasaki</a> has called the brand fanaticism "something that was stumbled upon,"<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> while Ive explained in 2014 that "People have an incredibly personal relationship" with Apple's products.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Apple_Store" title="Apple Store">Apple Store</a> openings can draw crowds of thousands, with some waiting in line as much as a day before the opening or flying in from other countries for the event.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> The opening of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Avenue" title="Fifth Avenue">Fifth Avenue</a> "Cube" store had a line half a mile long; a few Mac fans used the setting to propose marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> The line for the <a href="/wiki/Ginza" title="Ginza">Ginza</a> opening in Tokyo was estimated to include thousands of people and exceeded eight city blocks.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> The high level of brand loyalty has been criticized and ridiculed, applying the epithet "<a href="/wiki/Apple_fanboy" title="Apple fanboy">Apple fanboy</a>" and mocking the lengthy lines before a product launch.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup> An internal memo leaked in 2015 suggested the company planned to discourage long lines and direct customers to purchase its products on its website.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> magazine named Apple the most admired company in the United States in 2008, and in the world from 2008 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> On September 30, 2013, Apple surpassed <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> to become the world's most valuable brand in the <a href="/wiki/Omnicom_Group" title="Omnicom Group">Omnicom Group</a>'s "Best Global Brands" report.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boston_Consulting_Group" title="Boston Consulting Group">Boston Consulting Group</a> has ranked Apple as the world's most innovative brand every year since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>John Sculley told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> newspaper in 1997: "People talk about technology, but Apple was a marketing company. It was the marketing company of the decade."<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> Research in 2002 by <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Online" title="Nielsen Online">NetRatings</a> indicate that the average Apple consumer was usually more affluent and better educated than other PC company consumers. The research indicated that this correlation could stem from the fact that on average Apple Inc. products were more expensive than other PC products.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In response to a query about the devotion of loyal Apple consumers, Jonathan Ive responded:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>What people are responding to is much bigger than the object. They are responding to something rare—a group of people who do more than simply make something work, they make the very best products they possibly can. It’s a demonstration against thoughtlessness and carelessness.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_page">Home page</span></h3>
<p>The Apple website <a href="/wiki/Home_page" title="Home page">home page</a> has been used to commemorate, or pay tribute to, milestones and events outside of Apple's product offerings:</p>
<ul>
<li>2014: <a href="/wiki/Robin_Williams" title="Robin Williams">Robin Williams</a><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2013: <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2011: <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2010: <a href="/wiki/Jerry_York_(businessman)" title="Jerry York (businessman)">Jerome B. York</a> (board member)<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2007: <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2005: <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Parks" title="Rosa Parks">Rosa Parks</a><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2003: <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Hines" title="Gregory Hines">Gregory Hines</a><sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2001: <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apple_Campus" title="Apple Campus">Apple Campus</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg/220px-Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg/330px-Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg/440px-Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="511" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Apple_Campus_2_rendering.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A rendering of the Apple's under construction campus in Cupertino</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Apple Inc.'s world corporate headquarters are located in the middle of <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>, at 1–6 <a href="/wiki/Infinite_Loop_(street)" title="Infinite Loop (street)">Infinite Loop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cupertino,_California" title="Cupertino, California">Cupertino</a>, California. This Apple campus has six buildings that total 850,000 square feet (79,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) and was built in 1993 by Sobrato Development Cos.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Apple has a satellite campus in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Sunnyvale,_California" title="Sunnyvale, California">Sunnyvale, California</a>, where it houses a testing and research laboratory.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AppleInsider" title="AppleInsider" class="mw-redirect">AppleInsider</a> published article in March 2014 claiming that Apple has a tucked away a top-secret facility where is developing the SG5 electric vehicle project codenamed "Titan" under the shell company name <a href="/wiki/SixtyEight_Research" title="SixtyEight Research" class="mw-redirect">SixtyEight Research</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Apple announced its intention to build a second campus in Cupertino about 1 mile (1.6&#160;km) east of the current campus and next to Interstate 280.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> The new campus building will be designed by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster" title="Norman Foster" class="mw-redirect">Norman Foster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> The Cupertino City Council approved the proposed "spaceship" design campus on October 15, 2013, after a 2011 presentation by Jobs detailing the architectural design of the new building and its environs. The new campus is planned to house up to 13,000 employees in one central, four-storied, circular building surrounded by extensive landscape. It will feature a café with room for 3,000 sitting people and parking underground as well as in a parking structure. The 2.8 million square foot facility will also include Jobs's original designs for a fitness center and a corporate auditorium.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Apple's headquarters for Europe, the Middle East and Africa (EMEA) are located in <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a> in the south of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc17782206_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc17782206-272"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-humphries1_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-humphries1-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> The facility, which opened in 1980, was Apple's first location outside of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple Sales International, which deals with all of Apple's international sales outside of the USA, is located at Apple's campus in Cork<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup> along with Apple Distribution International, which similarly deals with Apple's international distribution network.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> On April 20, 2012, Apple added 500 new jobs at its European headquarters, increasing the total workforce from around 2,800 to 3,300 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-humphries1_273-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-humphries1-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup> The company will build a new office block on its Hollyhill Campus to accommodate the additional staff.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup> Its UK headquarters is at <a href="/wiki/Stockley_Park" title="Stockley Park">Stockley Park</a> on the outskirts of London.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2015, Apple opened their new 180,000-square-foot headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Herzliya" title="Herzliya">Herzliya</a>, Israel, which will accommodate approximately 800 employees. This opening was Apple's third office located within Israel; the first, also in Herzliya, was obtained as part of the Anobit acquisition, and the other is a research center in <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stores">Stores</span></h3>
<p>Apple has 453 retail stores (as of March 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-storenum_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-storenum-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> in 16 countries and an <a href="/wiki/Apple_Store_(online)" title="Apple Store (online)">online store</a> available in 39 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Apple_online_stores_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apple_online_stores-287"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup> Each store is designed to suit the needs of the location and regulatory authorities. Apple has received numerous architectural awards for its store designs, particularly its midtown Manhattan location on <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Avenue" title="Fifth Avenue">Fifth Avenue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fifth_Ave_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fifth_Ave-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IDSA_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDSA-289"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Apple Store in <a href="/wiki/Regent_Street" title="Regent Street">Regent Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, was the first to open in Europe in November 2004, and is the most profitable shop in London with the highest sales per square foot, taking £60,000,000 pa, or £2,000 per square foot.<sup id="cite_ref-Apple_Store_London_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apple_Store_London-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> The Regent Street store was surpassed in size by the nearby Apple Store in <a href="/wiki/Covent_Garden" title="Covent Garden">Covent Garden</a>, which was surpassed in size by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Terminal" title="Grand Central Terminal">Grand Central Terminal</a> Apple Store, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, in December 2011.</p>
<p>Of the 43,000 Apple employees in the United States 30,000 work at Apple Stores. Apple Store employees make above average pay for retail employees and are offered money toward college as well as gym memberships, 401k plans, healthcare plans, product discounts, and reduced price on purchase of stock.<sup id="cite_ref-9to5624_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9to5624-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 161.33333333333px">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mergers_and_acquisitions_by_Apple" title="List of mergers and acquisitions by Apple">List of mergers and acquisitions by Apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braeburn_Capital" title="Braeburn Capital">Braeburn Capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/FileMaker_Inc." title="FileMaker Inc.">FileMaker Inc.</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_culture">Corporate culture</span></h3>
<p>Apple was one of several highly successful companies founded in the 1970s that bucked the traditional notions of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_culture" title="Corporate culture" class="mw-redirect">corporate culture</a>. Jobs often walked around the office barefoot even after Apple became a <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> company. By the time of the "1984" television commercial, Apple's informal culture had become a key trait that differentiated it from its competitors.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup> According to a 2011 report in <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a>,</i> this has resulted in a corporate culture more akin to a startup rather than a multinational corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune1_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune1-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As the company has grown and been led by a series of differently opinionated chief executives, it has arguably lost some of its original character. Nonetheless, it has maintained a reputation for fostering individuality and excellence that reliably attracts talented workers, particularly after Jobs returned to the company. Numerous Apple employees have stated that projects without Jobs's involvement often take longer than projects with it.<sup id="cite_ref-cultofmacwork_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cultofmacwork-294"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup> To recognize the best of its employees, Apple created the Apple Fellows program which awards individuals who make extraordinary technical or leadership contributions to <a href="/wiki/Personal_computing" title="Personal computing" class="mw-redirect">personal computing</a> while at the company. The Apple Fellowship has so far been awarded to individuals including <a href="/wiki/Bill_Atkinson" title="Bill Atkinson">Bill Atkinson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-hertzfeld_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hertzfeld-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Capps" title="Steve Capps">Steve Capps</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup> Rod Holt,<sup id="cite_ref-hertzfeld_295-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hertzfeld-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Kay" title="Alan Kay">Alan Kay</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-yoyow_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yoyow-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Guy_Kawasaki" title="Guy Kawasaki">Guy Kawasaki</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-yoyow_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yoyow-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al_Alcorn" title="Al Alcorn" class="mw-redirect">Al Alcorn</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Don_Norman" title="Don Norman">Don Norman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-yoyow_297-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yoyow-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rich_Page" title="Rich Page">Rich Page</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-hertzfeld_295-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hertzfeld-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Wozniak" title="Steve Wozniak">Steve Wozniak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hertzfeld_295-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hertzfeld-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At Apple, employees are specialists who are not exposed to functions outside their area of expertise. Jobs saw this as a means of having "best-in-class" employees in every role. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Johnson_(businessman)" title="Ron Johnson (businessman)">Ron Johnson</a>—Senior Vice President of Retail Operations until November 1, 2011—was responsible for site selection, in-store service, and store layout, yet had no control of the inventory in his stores (this was done by Cook, who had a background in supply-chain management).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_301-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple is also known for strictly enforcing accountability. Each project has a "directly responsible individual," or "DRI" in Apple jargon.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune1_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune1-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> As an example, when iOS senior vice president <a href="/wiki/Scott_Forstall" title="Scott Forstall">Scott Forstall</a> refused to sign Apple's official apology for numerous errors in the redesigned <a href="/wiki/Apple_Maps" title="Apple Maps">Maps app</a>, he was forced to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike other major U.S. companies Apple provides a relatively simple compensation policy for executives that does not include perks enjoyed by other CEOs like country club fees or private use of company aircraft. The company typically grants stock options to executives every other year.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Customer_service">Customer service</span></h3>
<p>In 1999 Apple retained Eight Inc. as a strategic retail design partner and began creating the Apple retail stores. Tim Kobe of Eight Inc. prepared an "Apple Retail" white paper for Jobs, outlining the ability of separate Apple retail stores to directly drive the Apple brand experience—Kobe used their recently completed work with The North Face and Nike as a basis for the white paper.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The first two Apple Stores opened on May 19, 2001 in Tysons Corner, Virginia, and <a href="/wiki/Glendale,_California" title="Glendale, California">Glendale, California</a>. More than 7,700 people visited Apple’s first two stores in the opening weekend, spending a total of US$599,000.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Apple maintains 425 <a href="/wiki/Apple_Store" title="Apple Store">retail stores</a> in fourteen countries.<sup id="cite_ref-AppleRetailStoreList_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AppleRetailStoreList-305"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to Apple products, the stores sell third-party products like software titles, digital cameras, camcorders and handheld organizers.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A media article published in July 2013 provided details about Apple's "At-Home Apple Advisors" customer support program that serves as the corporation's call center. The advisors are employed within the U.S. and work remotely after undergoing a four-week training program and testing period. The advisors earn between US$9 and $12 per hour and receive intensive management to ensure a high quality of customer support.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</span></h3>
<p>The company's manufacturing, procurement and logistics enable it to execute massive product launches without having to maintain large, profit-sapping inventories. In 2011, Apple's profit margins were 40 percent, compared with between 10 and 20 percent for most other hardware companies. Cook's catchphrase to describe his focus on the company's operational arm is: “Nobody wants to buy sour milk”.<sup id="cite_ref-supply_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-supply-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span>[</span>309<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the Mac's early history Apple generally refused to adopt prevailing industry standards for hardware, instead creating their own.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310"><span>[</span>310<span>]</span></a></sup> This trend was largely reversed in the late 1990s, beginning with Apple's adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Peripheral_Component_Interconnect" title="Peripheral Component Interconnect" class="mw-redirect">PCI</a> bus in the <a href="/wiki/Power_Macintosh_7500" title="Power Macintosh 7500">7500</a>/<a href="/wiki/Power_Macintosh_8500" title="Power Macintosh 8500">8500</a>/<a href="/wiki/Power_Macintosh_9500" title="Power Macintosh 9500">9500</a> <a href="/wiki/Power_Macintosh" title="Power Macintosh">Power Macs</a>. Apple has since adopted (and often co-developed) industry standards such as <a href="/wiki/USB" title="USB">USB</a>, <a href="/wiki/AGP" title="AGP" class="mw-redirect">AGP</a>, <a href="/wiki/HyperTransport" title="HyperTransport">HyperTransport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a>, and others in its products. <a href="/wiki/FireWire" title="FireWire" class="mw-redirect">FireWire</a> is an Apple-originated standard that was widely adopted across the industry after it was standardized as <a href="/wiki/IEEE_1394" title="IEEE 1394">IEEE 1394</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311"><span>[</span>311<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_practices">Labor practices</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Apple_Inc.#Labor_practices" title="Criticism of Apple Inc.">Criticism of Apple Inc. § Labor practices</a></div>
<p>The company advertised its products as being made in America until the late 1990s; however, as a result of <a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">outsourcing</a> initiatives in the 2000s, almost all of its manufacturing is now handled abroad. According to a report by the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a></i>, Apple insiders "believe the vast scale of overseas factories as well as the flexibility, diligence and industrial skills of foreign workers have so outpaced their American counterparts that “Made in the U.S.A.” is no longer a viable option for most Apple products".<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312"><span>[</span>312<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, the <i><a href="/wiki/Mail_on_Sunday" title="Mail on Sunday" class="mw-redirect">Mail on Sunday</a></i> reported on the working conditions of the Chinese factories where contract manufacturers <a href="/wiki/Foxconn" title="Foxconn">Foxconn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inventec" title="Inventec">Inventec</a> produced the iPod.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313"><span>[</span>313<span>]</span></a></sup> The article stated that one complex of factories that assembled the iPod and other items had over 200,000 workers living and working within it. Employees regularly worked more than 60 hours per week and made around $100 per month. A little over half of the workers' earnings was required to pay for rent and food from the company.<sup id="cite_ref-wpsweatshop_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpsweatshop-314"><span>[</span>314<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315"><span>[</span>315<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316"><span>[</span>316<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Apple immediately launched an investigation after the 2006 media report, and worked with their manufacturers to ensure acceptable working conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317"><span>[</span>317<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, Apple started yearly audits of all its suppliers regarding <a href="/wiki/Worker%27s_rights" title="Worker's rights" class="mw-redirect">worker's rights</a>, slowly raising standards and pruning suppliers that did not comply. Yearly progress reports have been published since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318"><span>[</span>318<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, Apple admitted that its suppliers' child labor practices in China had worsened.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Foxconn_suicides" title="Foxconn suicides">Foxconn suicides</a> occurred between January and November 2010, when 18<sup id="cite_ref-tian_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tian-320"><span>[</span>320<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Foxconn" title="Foxconn">Foxconn</a> (Chinese: 富士康) employees attempted <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a>, resulting in 14 deaths—the company was the world’s largest contract electronics manufacturer, for clients including Apple, at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-tian_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tian-320"><span>[</span>320<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scmpreport_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmpreport-321"><span>[</span>321<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters3_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters3-322"><span>[</span>322<span>]</span></a></sup> The suicides drew media attention, and employment practices at Foxconn were investigated by Apple.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ-Foxconn_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-Foxconn-323"><span>[</span>323<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple issued a public statement about the suicides, and company spokesperson Steven Dowling said:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>[Apple is] saddened and upset by the recent suicides at Foxconn ... A team from Apple is independently evaluating the steps they are taking to address these tragic events and we will continue our ongoing inspections of the facilities where our products are made.<sup id="cite_ref-Huff_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Huff-324"><span>[</span>324<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The statement was released after the results from the company's probe into its suppliers' labor practices were published in early 2010. Foxconn was not specifically named in the report, but Apple identified a series of serious labor violations of labor laws, including Apple's own rules, and some child labor existed in a number of factories.<sup id="cite_ref-Huff_324-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Huff-324"><span>[</span>324<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple committed to the implementation of changes following the suicides.<sup id="cite_ref-Fire_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fire-325"><span>[</span>325<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2010, workers in China planned to sue iPhone contractors over poisoning by a cleaner used to clean LCD screens. One worker claimed that he and his coworkers had not been informed of possible occupational illnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326"><span>[</span>326<span>]</span></a></sup> After a high suicide rate in a Foxconn facility in China making iPads and iPhones, albeit a lower rate than that of China as a whole,<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327"><span>[</span>327<span>]</span></a></sup> workers were forced to sign a legally binding document guaranteeing that they would not kill themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328"><span>[</span>328<span>]</span></a></sup> Workers in factories producing Apple products have also been exposed to n-<a href="/wiki/Hexane" title="Hexane">hexane</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Neurotoxin" title="Neurotoxin">neurotoxin</a> that is a cheaper alternative than alcohol for cleaning the products.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329"><span>[</span>329<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330"><span>[</span>330<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331"><span>[</span>331<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/China_Labor_Watch" title="China Labor Watch">China Labor Watch</a> said it found violations of the law and of Apple's working condition pledges at facilities operated by <a href="/wiki/Pegatron" title="Pegatron">Pegatron</a>. These violations included discrimination against ethnic minorities and women, withholding of employee pay, excessive work hours, poor living conditions, health and safety problems and pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332"><span>[</span>332<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A 2014 BBC investigation found excessive hours and other problems persisted, despite Apple's promise to reform factory practice after the 2010 Foxconn suicides. The Pegatron factory was once again the subject of review, as reporters gained access to the working conditions inside through recruitment as employees. While the BBC maintained that the experiences of its reporters showed that labor violations were continuing since 2010, Apple publicly disagreed with the BBC and stated: “We are aware of no other company doing as much as Apple to ensure fair and safe working conditions".<sup id="cite_ref-Fire_325-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fire-325"><span>[</span>325<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Global_Labour_and_Human_Rights" title="Institute for Global Labour and Human Rights">Institute for Global Labour and Human Rights</a> published a report which documented inhumane conditions for the 15,000 workers at a Zhen Ding Technology factory in Shenzhen, China, which serves as a major supplier of circuit boards for Apple's iPhone and iPad. According to the report, workers are pressured into 65 hour work weeks which leaves them so exhausted that they often sleep during lunch breaks. They are also made to reside in "primitive, dark and filthy dorms" where they sleep "on plywood, with six to ten workers in each crowded room." Omnipresent security personnel also routinely harass and beat the workers.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333"><span>[</span>333<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334"><span>[</span>334<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_lawsuits_at_California_retail_stores">Employee lawsuits at California retail stores</span></h5>
<p>In a recent class action lawsuit in California approximately 12,400 former and current Apple retail store employees alleged they should have been compensated for having to wait in line and for undergoing off-the-clock security bag searches and clearance checks when they left work for meal breaks or at the end of their shifts.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335"><span>[</span>335<span>]</span></a></sup> The unpaid search practice started in 2009 over concerns of increasing employee theft and the employees claimed the searches were not efficiently conducted. The suit alleged illegal and improper wage practices in violation of the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Labor_Standards_Act" title="Fair Labor Standards Act">Fair Labor Standards Act</a> that deprived staff of wages they should have earned during what they contended was compensable time at "work". On November 7, 2015, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_California" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of California">United States District Court for the Northern District of California</a> issued an order granting Apple’s Motion for Summary Judgment dismissing each and every claim brought against Apple by the employees in this case.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336"><span>[</span>336<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="No_cold_calling_agreements_in_the_United_States">No cold calling agreements in the United States</span></h5>
<p>In 2013 <a href="/wiki/Hi-Tech_Employee_class_action_lawsuit" title="Hi-Tech Employee class action lawsuit" class="mw-redirect">class action against</a> several Silicon Valley companies, including Apple, was filed for alleged "no cold call” agreements which restrained the recruitment of high-tech employees.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337"><span>[</span>337<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_practices">Environmental practices</span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h5>
<p>Following a Greenpeace protest, Apple released a statement on April 17, 2012 committing to ending its use of coal and shifting to 100% clean energy.<sup id="cite_ref-After_Greenpeace_Protests.2C_Apple_Promises_to_Dump_Coal_Power_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-After_Greenpeace_Protests.2C_Apple_Promises_to_Dump_Coal_Power-338"><span>[</span>338<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Powering_Our_Facilities_with_Clean.2C_Renewable_Energy_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powering_Our_Facilities_with_Clean.2C_Renewable_Energy-339"><span>[</span>339<span>]</span></a></sup> By 2013 Apple was using 100% renewable energy to power their data centers. Overall, 75% of the company's power came from renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340"><span>[</span>340<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Climate_Counts" title="Climate Counts">Climate Counts</a>, a nonprofit organization dedicated to directing consumers toward the greenest companies, gave Apple a score of 52 points out of a possible 100, which puts Apple in their top category "Striding".<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341"><span>[</span>341<span>]</span></a></sup> This was an increase from May 2008, when Climate Counts only gave Apple 11 points out of 100, which placed the company last among electronics companies, at which time Climate Counts also labeled Apple with a "stuck icon", adding that Apple at the time was "a choice to avoid for the climate conscious consumer".<sup id="cite_ref-iwclimate_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iwclimate-342"><span>[</span>342<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Toxins">Toxins</span></h5>
<p>Following further campaigns by Greenpeace,<sup id="cite_ref-itox_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itox-343"><span>[</span>343<span>]</span></a></sup> in 2008 Apple became the first laptop manufacturer to eliminate the inclusion of <a href="/wiki/Polyvinyl_chloride" title="Polyvinyl chloride">PVC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brominated_flame_retardant" title="Brominated flame retardant">BFRs</a> in its devices.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344"><span>[</span>344<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345"><span>[</span>345<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2007, Apple began replacing the <a href="/wiki/Cold_cathode" title="Cold cathode">cold cathode</a> fluorescent lamp (CCFL) backlit <a href="/wiki/LCD" title="LCD" class="mw-redirect">LCD</a> displays in its computers with <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a>-free <a href="/wiki/LED" title="LED" class="mw-redirect">LED</a> backlit LCD displays and <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a>-free glass, starting with the upgraded <a href="/wiki/MacBook_Pro" title="MacBook Pro">MacBook Pro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Apple-environmental-news_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apple-environmental-news-346"><span>[</span>346<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-agreenapple_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agreenapple-347"><span>[</span>347<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-green_notebooks_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green_notebooks-348"><span>[</span>348<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349"><span>[</span>349<span>]</span></a></sup> Apple offers information about emissions, materials, and electrical usage concerning each product.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350"><span>[</span>350<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2009, Apple's iPhone 3GS was free of PVC, arsenic, and BFRs.<sup id="cite_ref-Apple-environmental-news_346-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apple-environmental-news-346"><span>[</span>346<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351"><span>[</span>351<span>]</span></a></sup> All Apple computers now have mercury free LED backlit displays, arsenic-free glass, and non-PVC cables. All Apple computers also have <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Product_Environmental_Assessment_Tool" title="Electronic Product Environmental Assessment Tool">Electronic Product Environmental Assessment Tool (EPEAT)</a> Gold status.<sup id="cite_ref-Apple-environmental-news_346-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Apple-environmental-news-346"><span>[</span>346<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2011, Chinese authorities ordered an Apple supplier to close part of its plant in <a href="/wiki/Suzhou" title="Suzhou">Suzhou</a> after residents living nearby raised significant environmental concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352"><span>[</span>352<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2011, Apple featured in Greenpeace's Guide to Greener Electronics, which ranks electronics manufacturers on sustainability, climate and energy policy, and how "green" their products are. The company ranked fourth of fifteen electronics companies (moving up five places from the previous year) with a score of 4.6/10 down from 4.9.<sup id="cite_ref-Guide_to_Greener_Electronics_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guide_to_Greener_Electronics-353"><span>[</span>353<span>]</span></a></sup> Greenpeace praises Apple's sustainability, noting that the company exceeded its 70% global recycling goal in 2010. It continues to score well on the products rating with all Apple products now being free of PVC vinyl plastic and brominated flame retardants. However, the guide criticizes Apple on the Energy criteria for not seeking external verification of its greenhouse gas emissions data and for not setting out any targets to reduce emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-Guide_to_Greener_Electronics_353-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guide_to_Greener_Electronics-353"><span>[</span>353<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2012, Apple requested that their cable maker, Volex, begin producing halogen-free USB and power cables.<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354"><span>[</span>354<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span></h3>
<p>Apple is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_information_technology_companies" title="List of the largest information technology companies">world's largest information technology company</a> by revenue and the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone#Manufacturers" title="Mobile phone">world's third-largest mobile phone maker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355"><span>[</span>355<span>]</span></a></sup> It is also the <a href="/wiki/List_of_corporations_by_market_capitalization" title="List of corporations by market capitalization" class="mw-redirect">largest publicly traded corporation in the world by market capitalization</a>, with an estimated market capitalization of $446 billion by January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Marketwatch_AAPL_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marketwatch_AAPL-356"><span>[</span>356<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 17, 2015, Apple became the first US corporation to be valued at over $750B.<sup id="cite_ref-Macs_4_Newbies_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macs_4_Newbies-357"><span>[</span>357<span>]</span></a></sup> As of December 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Apple maintains 447 <a href="/wiki/Apple_Store" title="Apple Store">retail stores</a> including 182 in fourteen countries, as well as the online <a href="/wiki/Apple_Store_(online)" title="Apple Store (online)">Apple Store</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>, the latter of which is the world's largest music retailer.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358"><span>[</span>358<span>]</span></a></sup> As of September 29, 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it employs 72,800 permanent full-time employees and 3,300 temporary full-time employees worldwide.</p>
<p>In its fiscal year ending in September 2011, Apple Inc. reported a total of $108 billion in annual revenues—a significant increase from its 2010 revenues of $65 billion—and nearly $82 billion in cash reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359"><span>[</span>359<span>]</span></a></sup> On March 19, 2012, Apple announced plans for a $2.65-per-share dividend beginning in fourth quarter of 2012, per approval by their board of directors.<sup id="cite_ref-dividendfaq_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dividendfaq-360"><span>[</span>360<span>]</span></a></sup> On September 2012, Apple reached a record share price of more than $705 and closed at above 700.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361"><span>[</span>361<span>]</span></a></sup> With 936,596,000 outstanding shares (as of June 30, 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>),<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362"><span>[</span>362<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The company's worldwide annual revenue in 2013 totaled $170 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363"><span>[</span>363<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 2013, Apple entered the top ten of the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of companies for the first time, rising 11 places above its 2012 ranking to take the sixth position.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364"><span>[</span>364<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Apple has around $200 billion of <a href="/wiki/Cash_and_cash_equivalents" title="Cash and cash equivalents">cash equivalents</a>, of which 90% is located outside the United States for tax purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-b200_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b200-365"><span>[</span>365<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_practices">Tax practices</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Apple_Inc.#Tax_practices" title="Criticism of Apple Inc.">Criticism of Apple Inc. § Tax practices</a></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="float:right;">
<caption>Global taxes paid by ASI, 2009–2011<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366"><span>[</span>366<span>]</span></a></sup></caption>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th scope="col">2011</th>
<th scope="col">2010</th>
<th scope="col">2009</th>
<th scope="col">Total</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Pre-tax earnings</th>
<td>US$22 billion</td>
<td>US$12 billion</td>
<td>US$4 billion</td>
<td>US$38 billion</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Global tax</th>
<td>US$10 million</td>
<td>US$7 million</td>
<td>US$4 million</td>
<td>US$21 million</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Tax rate</th>
<td>0.05%</td>
<td>0.06%</td>
<td>0.1%</td>
<td>0.06%</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Apple has created subsidiaries in low-tax places such as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> to cut the taxes it pays around the world. According to <i>The New York Times,</i> in the 1980s Apple was among the first tech companies to designate overseas salespeople in high-tax countries in a manner that allowed the company to sell on behalf of low-tax subsidiaries on other continents, sidestepping income taxes. In the late 1980s Apple was a pioneer of an accounting technique known as the "<a href="/wiki/Double_Irish_with_a_Dutch_sandwich" title="Double Irish with a Dutch sandwich" class="mw-redirect">Double Irish with a Dutch sandwich</a>," which reduces taxes by routing profits through Irish subsidiaries and the Netherlands and then to the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367"><span>[</span>367<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/British_Conservative_Party" title="British Conservative Party" class="mw-redirect">British Conservative Party</a> Member of Parliament <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Elphicke" title="Charlie Elphicke">Charlie Elphicke</a> published research on October 30, 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368"><span>[</span>368<span>]</span></a></sup> which showed that some multinational companies, including Apple Inc., were making billions of pounds of profit in the UK, but were paying an effective tax rate to the UK Treasury of only 3 percent, well below standard <a href="/wiki/Corporation_tax" title="Corporation tax" class="mw-redirect">corporation tax</a>. He followed this research by calling on the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Osborne" title="George Osborne">George Osborne</a> to force these multinationals, which also included <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">The Coca-Cola Company</a>, to state the effective rate of tax they pay on their UK revenues. Elphicke also said that government contracts should be withheld from multinationals who do not pay their fair share of UK tax.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369"><span>[</span>369<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2014 the <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Competition" title="European Commissioner for Competition">European Commissioner for Competition</a> launched an investigation of Apple's tax practices in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, as part of a wider probe of multi-national companies' tax arrangements in various European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-ECprobe_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECprobe-370"><span>[</span>370<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As part of the <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Leaks" title="Luxembourg Leaks">Luxembourg Leaks</a>, Apple was revealed to use the <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> tax haven for tax avoidance.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371"><span>[</span>371<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015 <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> reported that Apple had earnings abroad of $54.4 billion which were untaxed by the <a href="/wiki/IRS" title="IRS" class="mw-redirect">IRS</a>. Under U.S. law corporations don't pay income tax on overseas profits until the profits are brought into the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372"><span>[</span>372<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Litigation">Litigation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc._litigation" title="Apple Inc. litigation">Apple Inc. litigation</a></div>
<p>Apple has been a participant in various legal proceedings and claims since it began operation.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373"><span>[</span>373<span>]</span></a></sup> In particular, Apple is known for and promotes itself as actively and aggressively enforcing its intellectual property interests. Some litigation examples include <i><a href="/wiki/Apple_v._Samsung" title="Apple v. Samsung" class="mw-redirect">Apple v. Samsung</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Apple_v._Microsoft" title="Apple v. Microsoft" class="mw-redirect">Apple v. Microsoft</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility_v._Apple_Inc." title="Motorola Mobility v. Apple Inc.">Motorola Mobility v. Apple Inc.</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Apple_Corps_v._Apple_Computer" title="Apple Corps v. Apple Computer" class="mw-redirect">Apple Corps v. Apple Computer</a></i>. Apple has also had to defend itself against charges of violating other’s intellectual property rights. In October 2015, for example, a jury found that Apple had infringed a <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin" title="University of Wisconsin" class="mw-redirect">University of Wisconsin</a> patent on microprocessor technology.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374"><span>[</span>374<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charitable_causes">Charitable causes</span></h3>
<p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Apple_Inc.&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Apple is listed as a partner of the <a href="/wiki/Product_RED" title="Product RED" class="mw-redirect">Product RED</a> campaign. The campaign's mission is to prevent the transmission of <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> from mother to child by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375"><span>[</span>375<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2012, Apple donated $2.5 million to the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> to aid relief efforts after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376"><span>[</span>376<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
